That should be the common case.\\n258:         //      Simply commit that transaction in that case.\\n259:         //\\n260:         //  (2) there are multiple pending transactions because one previous\\n261:         //      checkpoint was skipped. That is a rare case, but can happen\\n262:         //      for example when:\\n263:         //\\n264:         //        - the master cannot persist the metadata of the last\\n265:         //          checkpoint (temporary outage in the storage system) but\\n266:         //          could persist a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\\n267:         //\\n268:         //        - other tasks could not persist their status during\\n269:         //          the previous checkpoint, but did not trigger a failure because they\\n270:         //          could hold onto their state and could successfully persist it in\\n271:         //          a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\\n272:         //\\n273:         //      In both cases, the prior checkpoint never reach a committed state, but\\n274:         //      this checkpoint is always expected to subsume the prior one and cover all\\n275:         //      changes since the last successful one. As a consequence, we need to commit\\n276:         //      all pending transactions.\\n277:         //\\n278:         //  (3) Multiple transactions are pending, but the checkpoint complete notification\\n279:         //      relates not to the latest. That is possible, because notification messages\\n280:         //      can be delayed (in an extreme case till arrive after a succeeding checkpoint\\n281:         //      was triggered) and because there can be concurrent overlapping checkpoints\\n282:         //      (a new one is started before the previous fully finished).\\n283:         //\\n284:         // ==> There should never be a case where we have no pending transaction here\\n285:         //\\n286: \\n287:         Iterator<Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>>> pendingTransactionIterator =\\n288: \\n364:     @Override\\n365:     public void initializeState(FunctionInitializationContext context) throws Exception {\\n366:         // when we are restoring state with pendingCommitTransactions, we don't really know whether\\n367:         // the\\n368:         // transactions were already committed, or whether there was a failure between\\n369:         // completing the checkpoint on the master, and notifying the writer here.\\n370: \\n371:         // (the common case is actually that is was already committed, the window\\n372:         // between the commit on the master and the notification here is very small)\\n373: \\n374:         // it is possible to not have any transactions at all if there was a failure before\\n375:         // the first completed checkpoint, or in case of a That should be the common case.\\n258:         //      Simply commit that transaction in that case.\\n259:         //\\n260:         //  (2) there are multiple pending transactions because one previous\\n261:         //      checkpoint was skipped. That is a rare case, but can happen\\n262:         //      for example when:\\n263:         //\\n264:         //        - the master cannot persist the metadata of the last\\n265:         //          checkpoint (temporary outage in the storage system) but\\n266:         //          could persist a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\\n267:         //\\n268:         //        - other tasks could not persist their status during\\n269:         //          the previous checkpoint, but did not trigger a failure because they\\n270:         //          could hold onto their state and could successfully persist it in\\n271:         //          a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\\n272:         //\\n273:         //      In both cases, the prior checkpoint never reach a committed state, but\\n274:         //      this checkpoint is always expected to subsume the prior one and cover all\\n275:         //      changes since the last successful one. As a consequence, we need to commit\\n276:         //      all pending transactions.\\n277:         //\\n278:         //  (3) Multiple transactions are pending, but the checkpoint complete notification\\n279:         //      relates not to the latest. That is possible, because notification messages\\n280:         //      can be delayed (in an extreme case till arrive after a succeeding checkpoint\\n281:         //      was triggered) and because there can be concurrent overlapping checkpoints\\n282:         //      (a new one is started before the previous fully finished).\\n283:         //\\n284:         // ==> There should never be a case where we have no pending transaction here\\n285:         //\\n286: \\n287:         Iterator<Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>>> pendingTransactionIterator =\\n288:                 pendingCommitTransactions.entrySet().iterator();\\n289:         Throwable firstError = null;\\n290: \\n291:         while (pendingTransactionIterator.hasNext()) {\\n292:             Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>> entry = pendingTransactionIterator.next();\\n293:             Long pendingTransactionCheckpointId = entry.getKey();\\n294:             TransactionHolder<TXN> pendingTransaction = entry.getValue();\\n295:             if (pendingTransactionCheckpointId > checkpointId) {\\n296:                 continue;\\n297:             }\\n298: \\n299:             LOG.info(\\n300:                     \\\"{} - checkpoint {} complete, committing transaction {} from checkpoint {}\\\",\\n301:                     name(),\\n302:                     checkpointId,\\n303:                     pendingTransaction,\\n304:                     pendingTransactionCheckpointId);\\n305: \\n306:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(pendingTransaction);\\n307:             try {\\n308:                 commit(pendingTransaction.handle);\\n309:             } catch (Throwable t) {\\n310:                 if (firstError == null) {\\n311:                     firstError = t;\\n312:                 }\\n313:             }\\n314: \\n315:             LOG.debug(\\\"{} - committed checkpoint transaction {}\\\", name(), pendingTransaction);\\n316: \\n317:             pendingTransactionIterator.remove();\\n318:         }\\n319: \\n320:         if (firstError != null) {\\n321:             throw new FlinkRuntimeException(\\n322:                     \\\"Committing one of transactions failed, logging first encountered failure\\\",\\n323:                     firstError);\\n324:         }\\n325:     }\\n326: \\n327:     @Override\\n328:     public void notifyCheckpointAborted(long checkpointId) {}\\n329: \\n330:     @Override\\n331:     public void snapshotState(FunctionSnapshotContext context) throws Exception {\\n332:         // this is like the pre-commit of a 2-phase-commit transaction\\n333:         // we are ready to commit and remember the transaction\\n334: \\n335:         long checkpointId = context.getCheckpointId();\\n336:         LOG.debug(\\n337:                 \\\"{} - checkpoint {} triggered, flushing transaction '{}'\\\",\\n338:                 name(),\\n339:                 context.getCheckpointId(),\\n340:                 currentTransactionHolder);\\n341: \\n342:         if (currentTransactionHolder != null) {\\n343:             preCommit(currentTransactionHolder.handle);\\n344: }\\n347: \\n348:         // no need to start new transactions after sink function is closed (no more input data)\\n349:         if (!finished) {\\n350:             currentTransactionHolder = beginTransactionInternal();\\n351:         } else {\\n352:             currentTransactionHolder = null;\\n353:         }\\n354:         LOG.debug(\\\"{} - started new transaction '{}'\\\", name(), \\n364:     @Override\\n365:     public void initializeState(FunctionInitializationContext context) throws Exception {\\n366:         // when we are restoring state with pendingCommitTransactions, we don't really know whether\\n367:         // the\\n368:         // transactions were already committed, or whether there was a failure between\\n369:         // completing the checkpoint on the master, and notifying the writer here.\\n370: \\n371:         // (the common case is actually that is was already committed, the window\\n372:         // between the commit on the master and the notification here is very small)\\n373: \\n374:         // it is possible to not have any transactions at all if there was a failure before\\n375:         // the first completed checkpoint, or in case of a scale-out event, where some of the\\n376:         // new task do not have and transactions assigned to check)\\n377: \\n378:         // we can have more than one transaction to check in case of a scale-in event, or\\n379:         // for the reasons discussed in the 'notifyCheckpointComplete()' method.\\n380: \\n381:         state = context.getOperatorStateStore().getListState(stateDescriptor);\\n382: \\n383:         boolean recoveredUserContext = false;\\n384:         if (context.isRestored()) {\\n385:             LOG.info(\\\"{} - restoring state\\\", name());\\n386:             for (State<TXN, CONTEXT> operatorState : state.get()) {\\n387:                 userContext = operatorState.getContext();\\n388: ArrayList<>(recoveredTransactions.size() + 1);\\n391:                 for (TransactionHolder<TXN> recoveredTransaction : recoveredTransactions) {\\n392:                     // If this fails to succeed eventually, there is actually data loss\\n393:                     recoverAndCommitInternal(recoveredTransaction);\\n394:                     handledTransactions.add(recoveredTransaction.handle);\\n395:                     LOG.info(\\\"{} committed recovered transaction {}\\\", name(), recoveredTransaction);\\n396:                 }\\n397: \\n398:                 {\\n399:                     if (operatorState.getPendingTransaction() != null) {\\n400:                         TXN transaction = operatorState.getPendingTransaction());\\n407:                     }\\n408:                 }\\n409: \\n410:                 if (userContext.isPresent()) {\\n411: restore we didn't get any userContext or we are initializing from scratch\\n418:         if (!recoveredUserContext) {\\n419:             LOG.info(\\\"{} - no state to restore\\\", name());\\n420: beginTransactionInternal() throws Exception {\\n434:         return new TransactionHolder<>(beginTransaction(), clock.millis());\\n435:     }\\n436: \\n437:     /**\\n438:      * This method must be   logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(transactionHolder);\\n445:             recoverAndCommit(transactionHolder.handle);\\n446:         } catch (final Exception e) {\\n447:             final long That should be the common case.\n258:         //      Simply commit that transaction in that case.\n259:         //\n260:         //  (2) there are multiple pending transactions because one previous\n261:         //      checkpoint was skipped. That is a rare case, but can happen\n262:         //      for example when:\n263:         //\n264:         //        - the master cannot persist the metadata of the last\n265:         //          checkpoint (temporary outage in the storage system) but\n266:         //          could persist a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\n267:         //\n268:         //        - other tasks could not persist their status during\n269:         //          the previous checkpoint, but did not trigger a failure because they\n270:         //          could hold onto their state and could successfully persist it in\n271:         //          a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\n272:         //\n273:         //      In both cases, the prior checkpoint never reach a committed state, but\n274:         //      this checkpoint is always expected to subsume the prior one and cover all\n275:         //      changes since the last successful one. As a consequence, we need to commit\n276:         //      all pending transactions.\n277:         //\n278:         //  (3) Multiple transactions are pending, but the checkpoint complete notification\n279:         //      relates not to the latest. That is possible, because notification messages\n280:         //      can be delayed (in an extreme case till arrive after a succeeding checkpoint\n281:         //      was triggered) and because there can be concurrent overlapping checkpoints\n282:         //      (a new one is started before the previous fully finished).\n283:         //\n284:         // ==> There should never be a case where we have no pending transaction here\n285:         //\n286: \n287:         Iterator<Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>>> pendingTransactionIterator =\n288:                 pendingCommitTransactions.entrySet().iterator();\n289:         Throwable firstError = null;\n290: \n291:         while (pendingTransactionIterator.hasNext()) {\n292:             Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>> entry = pendingTransactionIterator.next();\n293:             Long pendingTransactionCheckpointId = entry.getKey();\n294:             TransactionHolder<TXN> pendingTransaction = entry.getValue();\n295:             if (pendingTransactionCheckpointId > checkpointId) {\n296:                 continue;\n297:             }\n298: \n299:             LOG.info(\n300:                     \"{} - checkpoint {} complete, committing transaction {} from checkpoint {}\",\n301:                     name(),\n302:                     checkpointId,\n303:                     pendingTransaction,\n304:                     pendingTransactionCheckpointId);\n305: \n306:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(pendingTransaction);\n307:             try {\n308:                 commit(pendingTransaction.handle);\n309:             } catch (Throwable t) {\n310:                 if (firstError == null) {\n311:                     firstError = t;\n312:                 }\n313:             }\n314: \n315:             LOG.debug(\"{} - restoring state\", name());\n386:             for (State<TXN, CONTEXT> operatorState : state.get()) {\n387:                 userContext = operatorState.getContext();\n388:                 List<TransactionHolder<TXN>> recoveredTransactions =\n389:                         operatorState.getPendingCommitTransactions();\n390:                 List<TXN> handledTransactions = new ArrayList<>(recoveredTransactions.size() + 1);\n391:                 for (TransactionHolder<TXN> recoveredTransaction : recoveredTransactions) {\n392:                     // If this fails to succeed eventually, there is actually data loss\n393:                     recoverAndCommitInternal(recoveredTransaction);\n394:                     handledTransactions.add(recoveredTransaction.handle);\n395:                     LOG.info(\"{} committed recovered transaction {}\", name(), recoveredTransaction);\n396:                 }\n397: \n398:                 {\n399:                     if (operatorState.getPendingTransaction() != null) {\n400:                         TXN transaction = operatorState.getPendingTransaction().handle;\n401:                         recoverAndAbort(transaction);\n402:                         handledTransactions.add(transaction);\n403:                         LOG.info(\n404:                                 \"{} aborted recovered transaction {}\",\n405:                                 name(),\n406:                                 operatorState.getPendingTransaction());\n407:                     }\n408:                 }\n409: \n410:                 if (userContext.isPresent()) {\n411:                     finishRecoveringContext(handledTransactions);\n412:                     recoveredUserContext = true;\n413:                 }\n414:             }\n415:         }\n416: \n417:         // if in restore we didn't get any userContext or we are initializing from scratch\n418:         if (!recoveredUserContext) {\n419:             LOG.info(\"{} - started new transaction '{}'\", name(), currentTransactionHolder);\n427:     }\n428: \n429:     /**\n430:      * This method must be the only place to call {@link #beginTransaction()} to ensure that the\n431:      * {@link TransactionHolder} is created at the same time.\n432:      */\n433:     private TransactionHolder<TXN> beginTransactionInternal() throws Exception {\n434:         return new TransactionHolder<>(beginTransaction(), clock.millis());\n435:     }\n436: \n437:     /**\n438:      * This method must be the only place to call {@link #recoverAndCommit(Object)} to ensure that\n439:      * the configuration parameters {@link #transactionTimeout} and {@link\n440:      * #ignoreFailuresAfterTransactionTimeout} are respected.\n441:      */\n442:     private void recoverAndCommitInternal(TransactionHolder<TXN> transactionHolder) {\n443:         try {\n444:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(transactionHolder);\n445:             recoverAndCommit(transactionHolder.handle);\n446:         } catch (final Exception e) {\n447:             final long elapsedTime = clock.millis() - transactionHolder.transactionStartTime;\n448:             if (ignoreFailuresAfterTransactionTimeout && elapsedTime > transactionTimeout) {\n449:                 LOG.error(\n450:                         \"Error while committing transaction {}. \"\n451:                                 + \"Transaction has been open for longer than the transaction timeout ({}).\"\n452:                                 + \"Commit will not be attempted again. files within buckets. This is integrated\\n55:  * with the checkpointing mechanism to provide exactly once semantics.\\n56:  *\\n57:  * <p>When creating the sink a {@code basePath} must be specified. The base directory contains one\\n58:  * directory for every bucket. The bucket directories themselves contain several part files, with at\\n59:  * least one for each parallel subtask of the sink which is writing data to that bucket. These part\\n60:  * files contain the actual output data.\\n61:  *\\n62:  * <p>The sink uses a {@link BucketAssigner} to determine in which bucket directory each element\\n63:  * should be written to inside the base directory. The {@code BucketAssigner} can, for example, use\\n64:  * time or a property of the element to determine the bucket directory. The default {@code\\n65:  * BucketAssigner} is a {@link DateTimeBucketAssigner} which will create one new bucket every hour.\\n66:  * You can specify a custom {@code BucketAssigner} using the {@code\\n67:  * setBucketAssigner(bucketAssigner)} method, after calling {@link\\n68:  * StreamingFileSink#forRowFormat(Path, Encoder)} or {@link StreamingFileSink#forBulkFormat(Path,\\n69:  * BulkWriter.Factory)}.\\n70:  *\\n71:  * <p>The names of the part files could be defined using {@link OutputFileConfig}. This\\n72:  * configuration contains a part prefix and a part suffix that will be used with the parallel\\n73:  * subtask index of the sink and a rolling counter to determine the file names. For example with a\\n74:  * prefix \\\"prefix\\\" and a suffix \\\".ext\\\", a file named {@code \\\"prefix-1-17.ext\\\"} contains the data\\n75:  * from {@code subtask 1} of the sink and is the {@code 17th} bucket created by that subtask.\\n76:  *\\n77:  * <p>Part files roll based on the user-specified {@link RollingPolicy}. By default, a {@link\\n78:  * DefaultRollingPolicy} is used for row-encoded sink output; a {@link OnCheckpointRollingPolicy} is\\n79:  * used for bulk-encoded sink output.\\n80:  *\\n81:  * <p>In some scenarios, the open buckets are required to change based on time. In these cases, the\\n82:  * user can specify a {@code bucketCheckInterval} (by default 1m) and the sink will check\\n83:  * periodically and roll the part file if the specified rolling policy says so.\\n84:  *\\n85:  * <p>Part files can be in one of three states: {@code in-progress}, {@code pending} or {@code\\n86:  * finished}. The reason for this is how the sink works together with the checkpointing mechanism to\\n87:  * provide exactly-once semantics and fault-tolerance. The part file that is currently being written\\n88:  * to is {@code in-progress}. org.apache.flink.util.Preconditions;\\n49: \\n50: import java.io.IOException;\\n51: import java.io.Serializable;\\n52: \\n53: /**\\n54:  * Sink that emits its input elements to {@link FileSystem} files within buckets. This is integrated\\n55:  * with the checkpointing mechanism to provide exactly once semantics.\\n56:  *\\n57:  * <p>When creating the sink a {@code basePath} must be specified. The base directory contains one\\n58:  * directory for every bucket. The bucket directories themselves contain several part files, with at\\n59:  * least one for each parallel subtask of the sink which is writing data to that bucket. These part\\n60:  * files contain the actual output data.\\n61:  *\\n62:  * <p>The sink uses a {@link BucketAssigner} to determine in which bucket directory each element\\n63:  * should be written to inside the base directory. The {@code BucketAssigner} can, for example, use\\n64:  * time or a property of the element to determine the bucket directory. The default {@code\\n65:  * BucketAssigner} is a {@link DateTimeBucketAssigner} which will create one new bucket every hour.\\n66:  * You can specify a custom {@code BucketAssigner} using the {@code\\n67:  * setBucketAssigner(bucketAssigner)} method, after calling {@link\\n68:  * StreamingFileSink#forRowFormat(Path, Encoder)} or {@link StreamingFileSink#forBulkFormat(Path,\\n69:  * BulkWriter.Factory)}.\\n70:  *\\n71:  * <p>The names of the part files could be defined using {@link OutputFileConfig}. This\\n72:  * configuration contains a part prefix and a part suffix that will be used with the parallel\\n73:  * subtask index of the sink and a rolling counter to determine the file names. For example with a\\n74:  * prefix \\\"prefix\\\" and a suffix \\\".ext\\\", a file named {@code \\\"prefix-1-17.ext\\\"} contains the data\\n75:  * from {@code subtask 1} of the sink and is the {@code 17th} bucket created by that subtask.\\n76:  *\\n77:  * <p>Part files roll based on the user-specified {@link RollingPolicy}. By default, a {@link\\n78:  * DefaultRollingPolicy} is used for row-encoded sink output; a {@link OnCheckpointRollingPolicy} is\\n79:  * used for bulk-encoded sink output.\\n80:  *\\n81:  * <p>In some scenarios, the open buckets are required to change based on time. In these cases, the\\n82:  * user can specify a {@code bucketCheckInterval} (by default 1m) and the sink will check\\n83:  * periodically and roll the part file if the specified rolling policy says so.\\n84:  *\\n85:  * <p>Part files can be in one of three states: {@code in-progress}, {@code pending} or {@code\\n86:  * finished}. The reason for this is how the sink works together with the checkpointing mechanism to\\n87:  * provide exactly-once semantics and fault-tolerance. The part file that is currently being written\\n88:  * to is {@code in-progress}. Once a part file is closed for writing it becomes {@code pending}.\\n89:  * When a checkpoint is successful the currently pending files will be moved to {@code finished}.\\n90:  *\\n91:  * <p>If case of a failure, and in order to guarantee exactly-once semantics, the sink should roll\\n92:  * back to the state it had when that last successful checkpoint occurred. To this end, when\\n93:  * restoring, the restored files in {@code pending} state are transferred into the {@code finished}\\n94:  * state while any {@code in-progress} files are rolled back, so that they do not contain data that\\n95:  * arrived after the checkpoint from which we restore.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * @param <IN> Type of the elements emitted by this sink\\n98:  * @deprecated Use {@link org.apache.flink.connector.file.sink.FileSink} instead.\\n99:  */\\n100: @Internal\\n101: public class StreamingFileSink<IN> extends RichSinkFunction<IN>\\n102:         implements CheckpointedFunction, CheckpointListener {\\n103: \\n104:     private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L;\\n105: \\n106:     // ------------------------ configuration fields --------------------------\\n107: \\n108:     private final long bucketCheckInterval;\\n109: \\n110:     private final BucketsBuilder<IN, ?, ? \n50: import java.io.IOException;\n51: import java.io.Serializable;\n52: \n53: /**\n54:  * Sink that emits its input elements to {@link FileSystem} files within buckets. This is integrated\n55:  * with the checkpointing mechanism to provide exactly once semantics.\n56:  *\n57:  * <p>When creating the sink a {@code basePath} must be specified. The base directory contains one\n58:  * directory for every bucket. The bucket directories themselves contain several part files, with at\n59:  * least one for each parallel subtask of the sink which is writing data to that bucket. These part\n60:  * files contain the actual output data.\n61:  *\n62:  * <p>The sink uses a {@link BucketAssigner} to determine in which bucket directory each element\n63:  * should be written to inside the base directory. The {@code BucketAssigner} can, for example, use\n64:  * time or a property of the element to determine the bucket directory. The default {@code\n65:  * BucketAssigner} is a {@link DateTimeBucketAssigner} which will create one new bucket every hour.\n66:  * You can specify a custom {@code BucketAssigner} using the {@code\n67:  * setBucketAssigner(bucketAssigner)} method, after calling {@link\n68:  * StreamingFileSink#forRowFormat(Path, Encoder)} or {@link StreamingFileSink#forBulkFormat(Path,\n69:  * BulkWriter.Factory)}.\n70:  *\n71:  * <p>The names of the part files could be defined using {@link OutputFileConfig}. This\n72:  * configuration contains a part prefix and a part suffix that will be used with the parallel\n73:  * subtask index of the sink and a rolling counter to determine the file names. For example with a\n74:  * prefix \"prefix\" and a suffix \".ext\", a file named {@code \"prefix-1-17.ext\"} contains the data\n75:  * from {@code subtask 1} of the sink and is the {@code 17th} bucket created by that subtask.\n76:  *\n77:  * <p>Part files roll based on the user-specified {@link RollingPolicy}. By default, a {@link\n78:  * DefaultRollingPolicy} is used for row-encoded sink output; a {@link OnCheckpointRollingPolicy} is\n79:  * used for bulk-encoded sink output.\n80:  *\n81:  * <p>In some scenarios, the open buckets are required to change based on time. In these cases, the\n82:  * user can specify a {@code bucketCheckInterval} (by default 1m) and the sink will check\n83:  * periodically and roll the part file if the specified rolling policy says so.\n84:  *\n85:  * <p>Part files can be in one of three states: {@code in-progress}, {@code pending} or {@code\n86:  * finished}. The reason for this is how the sink works together with the checkpointing mechanism to\n87:  * provide exactly-once semantics and fault-tolerance. The part file that is currently being written\n88:  * to is {@code in-progress}. Once a part file is closed for writing it becomes {@code pending}.\n89:  * When a checkpoint is successful the currently pending files will be moved to {@code finished}.\n90:  *\n91:  * <p>If case of a failure, and in order to guarantee exactly-once semantics, the sink should roll\n92:  * back to the state it had when that last successful checkpoint occurred. To this end, when\n93:  * restoring, the restored files in {@code pending} state are transferred into the {@code finished}\n94:  * state while any {@code in-progress} files are rolled back, so that they do not contain data that\n95:  * arrived after the checkpoint from which we restore.\n96:  *\n97:  * @param <IN> Type of the elements emitted by this sink\n98:  * @deprecated Use {@link org.apache.flink.connector.file.sink.FileSink} instead.\n99:  */\n100: @Internal\n101: public class StreamingFileSink<IN> extends RichSinkFunction<IN>\n102:         implements CheckpointedFunction, CheckpointListener {\n103: \n104:     private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L;\n105: \n106:     // ------------------------ configuration fields --------------------------\n107: \n108:     private final long bucketCheckInterval;\n109: \n110:     private final BucketsBuilder<IN, ?, ?
